\label{def:hodge-bundle}
\index{Hodge bundle|textbf}
The \emph{Hodge bundle} $\mathbb{E} \to \overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$ is the rank-$g$ vector bundle whose fiber over $[(\Sigma_g; p_1, \ldots, p_n)]$ is:
\begin{equation}
\mathbb{E}_{[\Sigma_g]} = H^0(\Sigma_g, \Omega^1_{\Sigma_g})
\end{equation}
the space of holomorphic differentials.

The Chern classes:
\begin{equation}
\lambda_i = c_i(\mathbb{E}) \in H^{2i}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}, \mathbb{Q})
\end{equation}
are the \emph{$\lambda$-classes}. (The \emph{Mumford--Morita--Miller classes} $\kappa_i = \pi_*(\psi_{n+1}^{i+1}) \in H^{2i}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$ are related but distinct: they are pushforwards of powers of the universal cotangent class.)
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Faber--Pandharipande formula {\cite{FP00}}; \ClaimStatusProvedElsewhere]
\label{thm:mumford-formula}
\index{Faber--Pandharipande formula}
The top $\lambda$-class, paired with the appropriate $\psi$-class, evaluates to:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:faber-pandharipande}
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}} \psi_1^{2g-2}\,\lambda_g = \frac{2^{2g-1}-1}{2^{2g-1}} \cdot \frac{|B_{2g}|}{(2g)!}
\end{equation}
where $B_{2g}$ are Bernoulli numbers (Faber--Pandharipande~\cite{FP00}).  The integrand has degree $(2g-2)+g = 3g-2 = \dim\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}$.  At $g = 1$: $\frac{1}{2} \cdot \frac{1/6}{2} = \frac{1}{24}$; at $g = 2$: $\frac{7}{8} \cdot \frac{1/30}{24} = \frac{7}{5760}$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Imported-proof dependency tags]
\emph{Dependency tags.}
\begin{enumerate}[label=(D\arabic*)]
\item The class-theoretic setup is provided by
Theorem~\ref{thm:mmm-classes} and Definition~\ref{def:hodge-bundle}.
\item The closed-form Bernoulli expression is imported from the external
tautological-ring literature (see~\cite{Mumford83}).
\item In this manuscript, the formula is used as input to obstruction and
quantum-correction bookkeeping (e.g. Theorem~\ref{thm:obstruction-general}).
\end{enumerate}
\emph{Provenance note.}
This claim is used in this manuscript as an external theorem, proved in
\cite{Mumford83}. It is not reproved internally here.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Quantum obstructions as cohomology classes}

\begin{theorem}[Obstruction theory for quantum corrections; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:obstruction-quantum}
For a chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ and deformation parameter $t$, the obstruction to extending from genus $g-1$ to genus $g$ lies in:
\begin{equation}
\text{Obs}^{(g)}(\mathcal{A}) \in H^2(\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A}), \mathcal{Z}(\mathcal{A}))
\end{equation}
where $\mathcal{Z}(\mathcal{A})$ is the center of $\mathcal{A}$ viewed as a sheaf on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.

Explicitly, $\text{Obs}^{(1)}(\mathcal{A})$ captures central extensions and $\text{Obs}^{(g)}(\mathcal{A})$ for $g \geq 2$ captures higher genus anomalies.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Consider the Leray spectral sequence for the bar complex sheaf on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$:
\begin{equation}
E_2^{p,q} = H^p(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{H}^q(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))) \Rightarrow H^{p+q}(\bar{B}^{\text{global}}(\mathcal{A}))
\end{equation}
The obstruction to extending from genus $g-1$ to genus $g$ is the $d_2$ differential:
\begin{equation}
d_2: E_2^{0,1} \to E_2^{2,0}
\end{equation}
which measures the failure of local sections of the bar complex to extend globally over $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.
For central elements, $\mathcal{H}^0(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})) = \mathcal{Z}(\mathcal{A})$ (the center acts trivially on the bar differential), so the obstruction lands in $E_2^{2,0} = H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\mathcal{A}))$. The two cases follow: at $g=1$, $H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}, \mathbb{C}) \cong \mathbb{C}$ captures the central extension; for $g \geq 3$, $H^2(\mathcal{M}_g) \cong \mathbb{Q}$ by Harer stability, while $H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ has additional boundary classes (e.g., $\dim H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2) = 3$).
\end{proof}

\subsection{Explicit computation for small genus}

\begin{example}[Genus-1 obstruction]
\label{ex:genus-1-obstruction-complete}
For $g=1$, the coarse moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$ is isomorphic to $\mathbb{P}^1$ (the $j$-line, compactified by the nodal rational curve at $j = \infty$); as a Deligne--Mumford stack it is $[\overline{\mathcal{H}}/\mathrm{SL}_2(\mathbb{Z})]$ with $\dim_{\mathbb{C}} = 1$.  The Hodge class $\lambda = c_1(\mathbb{E})$ generates $\mathrm{Pic}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})_{\mathbb{Q}}$ with $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \lambda = 1/24$.

The cohomology is:
\begin{equation}
H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}) = \mathbb{Q}[\lambda] / (\lambda^2) \cong \mathbb{Q} \oplus \mathbb{Q}\lambda
\end{equation}

For the Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$, the obstruction to genus-1 extension defines a class in $H^2$:
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{obs}_1 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_1 \in H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}, \mathbb{C}) \cong \mathbb{C}
\end{equation}
(Note: $H^1(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}) = 0$ since the Poincar\'e polynomial $1 + t^2$ has no odd-degree terms.)

The \emph{central charge} is the numerical invariant:
\begin{equation}
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \mathrm{obs}_1 = \kappa \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}} \lambda_1 = \frac{\kappa}{24}
\end{equation}
\end{example}

\begin{example}[Genus 2 obstruction]
\label{ex:genus-2-obstruction}
For $g=2$, the moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2$ has dimension 3. The cohomology begins:
\begin{equation}
H^1(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2) = 0, \quad H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2) \cong \mathbb{Q}^{\oplus 3}
\end{equation}

Genus-2 quantum corrections for a chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ give classes:
\begin{equation}
[c_2] \in H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2, \mathcal{Z}(\mathcal{A}))
\end{equation}

For W-algebras, these involve \emph{screening charges} and \emph{higher central charges}.
\end{example}

% ================================================================
% PATCH 022: OBSTRUCTION CLASS COMPUTATION - EXPLICIT FORMULAS
% ================================================================

\section{Obstruction classes: explicit computation for all examples}
\label{sec:obstruction-explicit}

The obstruction class $\text{obs}_k \in H^2(B_g, Z(\mathcal{A}))$ admits explicit formulas for all key examples.

\subsection{Recollection: obstruction theory framework}
\label{subsec:obstruction-framework-recall}

\begin{definition}[Genus-\texorpdfstring{$g$}{g} obstruction class]\label{def:genus-g-obstruction}
\index{obstruction class|textbf}
For a chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ on a smooth curve $X$, the genus-$g$
obstruction to the bar differential squaring to zero is:
\[\text{obs}_g \in H^2(\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A}), Z(\mathcal{A}))\]
where:
\begin{itemize}
\item $\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A})$ is the genus-$g$ bar complex
\item $Z(\mathcal{A})$ is the center of $\mathcal{A}$
\item The class $[\text{obs}_g]$ measures the failure of $\dfib^{\,2} = 0$ on a fixed $\Sigma_g$
\end{itemize}
The superscript ``$H^2$'' here refers to \emph{bar complex degree}~$2$ (the bar differential has degree~$+1$, so $d \circ d$ lands in degree~$2$).  Under the Leray spectral sequence for $\overline{\mathcal{C}}_{g,n} \to \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$, this bar-degree-$2$ class maps to a class in $H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality} below), because $\lambda_g \in H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.  The two degrees should not be confused.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Obstruction formula; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:obstruction-general}
\textup{[Regime: curved-central
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

The genus-$g$ obstruction is computed by:
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{obs}_g = \sum_{\substack{g_1+g_2=g \\ g_1, g_2 \geq 1}} d_{g_1} \circ d_{g_2}
\end{equation}
where $d_{g'}$ is the genus-$g'$ component of the bar differential.  The condition $d_{\mathrm{total}}^2 = 0$ at order $\hbar^{2g-4}$ requires $[d_0, d_g] + \mathrm{obs}_g = 0$, so $d_g$ exists if and only if $\mathrm{obs}_g$ is a $d_0$-coboundary. The obstruction class $[\mathrm{obs}_g] \in H^2(\bar{B}_0(\mathcal{A}), Z(\mathcal{A}))$ is well-defined (independent of choices) and lands in the center by the argument in Step~4 below.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof of formula]

\emph{Step 1: Genus stratification of the differential.}

The full bar differential decomposes as:
\[d_{\text{total}} = \sum_{g=0}^{\infty} \hbar^{2g-2} d_g\]
(We use the closed-string convention $\hbar^{2g-2}$; the Feynman-diagram convention in \S\ref{sec:feynman_genus_g} uses $\hbar^{g-1}$, corresponding to $\hbar_{\text{there}} = \hbar_{\text{here}}^2$.)

Each $d_g$ involves integration over $g$-loop configuration spaces:
\[d_g = \sum_{n \geq 1} \int_{\overline{C}_n^{(g)}(X)} \text{Res}_{D} \circ \eta_g\]

\emph{Step~2: Squaring the differential.}

Compute $d_{\mathrm{total}}^2$:
\begin{align*}
d_{\text{total}}^2 &= \left(\sum_{g} \hbar^{2g-2} d_g\right)^2 \\
&= \sum_{g_1, g_2} \hbar^{2(g_1+g_2)-4} d_{g_1} \circ d_{g_2}
\end{align*}

At genus $g$ (i.e., coefficient of $\hbar^{2g-4}$), the condition $d_{\text{total}}^2 = 0$ gives:
\[\sum_{\substack{g_1 + g_2 = g \\ g_1, g_2 \geq 0}} d_{g_1} d_{g_2} = 0\]
Expanding: $d_0 d_g + d_1 d_{g-1} + \cdots + d_{g-1} d_1 + d_g d_0 = 0$.

\emph{Step 3: Arnold relations at genus zero.}

At genus zero, $d_0^2 = 0$ by the Arnold relations (Theorem~\ref{thm:arnold-three}).
For $g \geq 1$, the genus-$g$ condition $\sum_{g_1+g_2=g} d_{g_1}d_{g_2} = 0$ becomes $[d_0, d_g] = -\sum_{\substack{g_1+g_2=g \\ g_1,g_2 \geq 1}} d_{g_1}d_{g_2}$.  The obstruction comes from the right-hand side: the lower-genus differentials determine a constraint on $d_g$.

\emph{Step 4: Central elements.}

The obstruction $\operatorname{obs}_g = \sum_{\substack{g_1+g_2=g \\ g_1,g_2 \geq 1}} d_{g_1} \circ d_{g_2}$ lands in the center $Z(\mathcal{A})$.  For centrality, we use two facts.  First, $[d_0, \operatorname{obs}_g] = 0$ by the genus-$(g{+}1)$ condition from Step~2, so $\operatorname{obs}_g$ is a $d_0$-cocycle in $\mathrm{End}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A}))$ and defines a class in $H^0(\mathrm{End}(\bar{B}(\mathcal{A})), [d_0, -])$.  Second, each $d_{g_i}$ ($g_i \geq 1$) is constructed from period integrals $\oint_{\gamma_k} \omega$ over homology cycles $\gamma_k \subset \Sigma_g$.  These are \emph{global} operations on the curve, while the chiral bracket $\mu: \mathcal{A} \boxtimes \mathcal{A} \to \Delta_*\mathcal{A}$ is \emph{local} (supported on the diagonal).  By the locality axiom of chiral algebras, global operations on disjoint supports commute with local operations: $[\oint_{\gamma_k}, \mu(a, -)] = 0$ for any $a \in \mathcal{A}$, provided $\gamma_k$ does not pass through the collision locus.  Therefore $\operatorname{obs}_g$ commutes with all chiral products, hence is central.

\emph{Step 5: Moduli space integration.}

The genus-$g$ correction form $\omega_g$ appears through period integrals:
\[\omega_g = \int_{\gamma \in H_1(\Sigma_g)} \eta \wedge \bar{\eta}\]

Combining with Step 2 gives the stated formula.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Example 1: Heisenberg algebra -- level shift obstruction}
\label{subsec:heisenberg-obstruction}

\begin{theorem}[Heisenberg obstruction at genus \texorpdfstring{$g$}{g}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:heisenberg-obs}
For the Heisenberg vertex algebra $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ at level $\kappa$, the 
genus-$g$ obstruction is:
\begin{equation}
\text{obs}_g^{\mathcal{H}} = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g \in H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathbb{C})
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E})$ is the top Chern class of the Hodge bundle.

Explicitly:
\begin{itemize}
\item $g=1$: $\text{obs}_1 = \kappa \cdot [\tau]$ where $[\tau] \in H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1)$
\item $g=2$: $\text{obs}_2 = \kappa \cdot \lambda_2 = \kappa \cdot c_2(\mathbb{E})$
\item $g \geq 3$: $\text{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$
\end{itemize}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}

\emph{Step 1: Heisenberg structure.}

The Heisenberg algebra has generators $a_n$ with:
\[[a_m, a_n] = \kappa \cdot m \cdot \delta_{m+n,0} \cdot c\]
where $c$ is the central element.

\emph{Step 2: Bar differential at genus $g$.}

For $a_m \in \mathcal{H}_\kappa$, the genus-$g$ bar differential is:
\begin{align}
d_g(a_m) &= \sum_{k=-\infty}^{\infty} \int_{\overline{C}_2^{(g)}} a_k \otimes a_{m-k} 
\otimes \eta_{12}^{(g)} \\
&= \sum_{k} \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} a_k \otimes a_{m-k} \otimes 
\left(\int_{\Sigma_g} \text{d}\log\theta_1(z_{12}; \Omega_g)\right)
\end{align}

\emph{Step 3: Squaring the fiberwise differential.}

Compute $\dfib^{\,2}(a_m)$ on a fixed $\Sigma_g$:
\begin{align}
\dfib^{\,2}(a_m) &= \dfib\!\left(\sum_k \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} a_k \otimes a_{m-k} \otimes \omega_g\right) \\
&= \sum_{k_1, k_2} \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} [a_{k_1}, a_{k_2}] \otimes a_{m-k_1-k_2}
\otimes \omega_g^2
\end{align}

\emph{Step 4: Commutator evaluation.}

Using $[a_{k_1}, a_{k_2}] = \kappa \cdot k_1 \cdot \delta_{k_1 + k_2, 0} \cdot c$,
the Kronecker delta forces $k_2 = -k_1$, so
$a_{m - k_1 - k_2} = a_m$.  The remaining sum
$\sum_{k} k$ over mode indices is evaluated geometrically:
in the D-module formulation, the mode sum computes the
first Chern class of the direct image sheaf $R^0\pi_*\omega_{\mathcal{C}/\mathcal{M}_g}$
via the Quillen determinant anomaly formula~\cite{Quillen85}.  The result is:
\begin{equation}
\dfib^{\,2}(a_m) = \kappa \cdot a_m \otimes \lambda_g
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E}) \in H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.

\emph{Step 5: Evaluation of the obstruction class.}

At genus~$1$: the moduli space $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1$ has complex dimension~$1$, so $\lambda_1 = c_1(\mathbb{E})$ is a top-degree class, and the integral $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1} \lambda_1 = 1/24$ (the degree of the Hodge bundle).

At genus~$g \geq 2$: $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E})$ has degree~$g < 3g{-}3 = \dim_{\mathbb{C}}\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$, so the obstruction class $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ is a non-trivial class in $H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ but is \emph{not} a top-degree class.  Its numerical evaluation requires pairing with a complementary tautological class of degree~$2g{-}3$; the relevant intersection numbers are computable from the Faber conjectures (proved by Faber--Pandharipande) involving Bernoulli numbers.

\emph{Step 6: Obstruction class.}

Therefore:
\[\text{obs}_g^{\mathcal{H}} = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g\]

This is indeed a central element (proportional to $c$), confirming the consistency.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Physical interpretation: anomaly]\label{rem:heisenberg-anomaly}
The obstruction class $\text{obs}_g$ is the conformal anomaly at genus $g$.  The Bernoulli numbers $B_{2g}$ in Mumford's formula govern both the arithmetic of $\zeta(2g)$ and the geometry of $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Example 2: Kac--Moody algebras -- level and dual Coxeter number}
\label{subsec:kac-moody-obstruction}

\begin{theorem}[Kac--Moody obstruction at genus \texorpdfstring{$g$}{g}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:kac-moody-obs}
For the affine Kac--Moody vertex algebra $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ at level $k \neq -h^\vee$,
the genus-$g$ obstruction is:
\begin{equation}
\text{obs}_g^{\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}} = \frac{(k + h^\vee) \cdot
\text{dim}(\mathfrak{g})}{2h^\vee} \cdot \lambda_g
\end{equation}
where $h^\vee$ is the dual Coxeter number of $\mathfrak{g}$ and $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E})$
is the top Chern class of the Hodge bundle on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.

For specific Lie algebras:
\begin{align}
\mathfrak{g} = \mathfrak{sl}_2: \quad \text{obs}_g &= \frac{3(k+2)}{4} \lambda_g \\
\mathfrak{g} = \mathfrak{sl}_3: \quad \text{obs}_g &= \frac{4(k+3)}{3} \lambda_g \\
\mathfrak{g} = E_8: \quad \text{obs}_g &= \frac{62(k+30)}{15} \lambda_g
\end{align}

At the critical level $k = -h^\vee$, the obstruction vanishes for all $g$, consistent with
$d^2 = 0$ on the bar complex (Proposition~\ref{prop:km-bar-curvature}(i)).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}

\emph{Step 1: Genus-zero curvature.}

By Proposition~\ref{prop:km-bar-curvature}, the bar complex
of $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ has curvature:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:km-curvature-recall}
m_0 = \frac{k + h^\vee}{2h^\vee} \cdot \kappa
\end{equation}
where $\kappa = \sum_a J^a \otimes J_a$ is the Casimir element.  This curvature arises
because squaring the bar differential on degree-2 elements produces:
\[d^2(J^a \boxtimes J^b \cdot \eta_{12}) = (k + h^\vee) \cdot
\bigl(\text{adjoint Casimir contribution}\bigr)\]
The factor $h^\vee$ comes from the contraction
$\sum_c f^{ac}{}_d f^{bc}{}_e = 2h^\vee \cdot (J^a, J^b)$
(the Casimir eigenvalue on the adjoint representation in the normalization where
long roots have squared length 2).

\emph{Step 2: Extension to genus $g$.}

By the general obstruction formula (Theorem~\ref{thm:obstruction-general}), the genus-$g$
obstruction is:
\[\text{obs}_g = \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} \omega_g \otimes m_0\]
For $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$, the curvature element $m_0$ from Step~1 acts on each of the $\dim(\mathfrak{g})$ current generators.
The integration over $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ produces the Hodge class $\lambda_g$
by the same mechanism as in the Heisenberg case (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs}, Step~5):
the integral $\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} \omega_g^2 = \lambda_g$ via Mumford's formula.

\emph{Step 3: Assembling the formula.}

Each generator $J^a$ contributes a copy of the curvature $m_0$.  Summing over
$a = 1, \ldots, \dim(\mathfrak{g})$ and noting that $\kappa$ evaluated on the trace gives
$\sum_a (J^a, J_a) = \dim(\mathfrak{g})$:
\begin{align}
\text{obs}_g &= \dim(\mathfrak{g}) \cdot m_0 \cdot \lambda_g \\
&= \dim(\mathfrak{g}) \cdot \frac{k+h^\vee}{2h^\vee} \cdot \lambda_g \\
&= \frac{(k+h^\vee)\dim(\mathfrak{g})}{2h^\vee} \cdot \lambda_g
\end{align}

\emph{Step 4: Consistency checks.}

\emph{Critical level}: At $k = -h^\vee$, $\text{obs}_g = 0$ for all $g$. This is consistent
with $d^2 = 0$ on the bar complex at critical level (Proposition~\ref{prop:km-bar-curvature}(i)),
which reflects the enlarged center of $V_{-h^\vee}(\mathfrak{g})$.

\emph{Heisenberg limit}: Taking $\mathfrak{g}$ abelian (so $h^\vee = 0$ requires care),
we instead note that for the Heisenberg algebra the structure constants vanish ($f^{abc} = 0$),
so the Casimir correction is absent.  The obstruction reduces to
$\text{obs}_g = k \cdot \lambda_g$, in agreement with Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs}.

\emph{Koszul duality}: Under the Feigin--Frenkel involution $k \mapsto -k-2h^\vee$, the
obstruction transforms as:
\[\text{obs}_g^{\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{-k-2h^\vee}} =
\frac{(-k-2h^\vee+h^\vee)\dim(\mathfrak{g})}{2h^\vee} \cdot \lambda_g
= \frac{-(k+h^\vee)\dim(\mathfrak{g})}{2h^\vee} \cdot \lambda_g
= -\text{obs}_g^{\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k}\]
The sign reversal is consistent with Main~Theorem~C (Theorem~\ref{thm:quantum-complementarity-main}; the Kodaira--Spencer construction of Theorem~\ref{thm:kodaira-spencer-chiral-complete} provides the geometric mechanism):
what $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ sees as obstruction, $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{-k-2h^\vee}$
sees as the negative obstruction, confirming deformation-obstruction complementarity.

\emph{Step 5: Verification for $\mathfrak{sl}_2$.}

For $\mathfrak{sl}_2$: $\dim(\mathfrak{sl}_2) = 3$, $h^\vee = 2$,
$c_{\mathfrak{sl}_2, k} = 3k/(k+2)$.

The obstruction is:
\[\text{obs}_g = \frac{(k+2) \cdot 3}{2 \cdot 2} \lambda_g = \frac{3(k+2)}{4} \lambda_g\]

At genus 1 with $k=1$:
\[\text{obs}_1 = \frac{3 \cdot 3}{4} \lambda_1 = \frac{9}{4} \lambda_1\]

Numerically:
\[\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1} \lambda_1 = \frac{1}{24}\]

Therefore
\[\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1} \text{obs}_1 = \frac{9}{4} \cdot \frac{1}{24}
= \frac{3}{32}\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Level-rank duality]\label{rem:level-rank-obstruction}
The obstruction formula exhibits level-rank duality explicitly. For $\mathfrak{sl}_N$
at level $k$ (with $h^\vee(\mathfrak{sl}_N) = N$, $\dim(\mathfrak{sl}_N) = N^2-1$):
\[\text{obs}_g^{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_N(k)} =
\frac{(k+N) \cdot (N^2-1)}{2N} \cdot \lambda_g\]

Under level-rank duality $\mathfrak{sl}_N(k) \leftrightarrow \mathfrak{sl}_k(N)$:
\[\text{obs}_g^{\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_k(N)} =
\frac{(N+k) \cdot (k^2-1)}{2k} \cdot \lambda_g\]

The common factor $(N+k)$ is symmetric, while the remaining factors
$(N^2-1)/N$ and $(k^2-1)/k$ are exchanged under $N \leftrightarrow k$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Example 3: $\mathcal{W}$-algebras -- central charge dependence}
\label{subsec:w-algebra-obstruction}

\begin{theorem}[\texorpdfstring{$W_3$}{W3} obstruction with central charge; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:w3-obstruction}
For the $W_3$ algebra with generators $T$ (weight 2) and $W$ (weight 3) at 
central charge $c$, the genus-$g$ obstruction has the form:
\begin{equation}
\text{obs}_g^{W_3} = \left(\frac{c}{2} \cdot \lambda_g^{(T)} + 
\frac{c}{3} \cdot \lambda_g^{(W)}\right)
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_g^{(T)} := \lambda_g^{(2)} = c_g(R^0\pi_*\omega^{\otimes 2})$ and
$\lambda_g^{(W)} := \lambda_g^{(3)} = c_g(R^0\pi_*\omega^{\otimes 3})$ are the top
Chern classes of the bundles of $h$-differentials for $h = 2$ (Virasoro) and $h = 3$
(weight-$3$ generator), and the coefficients $c/2$, $c/3$ come from the leading OPE
singularities $T(z)T(w) \sim (c/2)/(z-w)^4 + \cdots$ and
$W(z)W(w) \sim (c/3)/(z-w)^6 + \cdots$.

For minimal models with $c = 2(1 - \frac{12(p-q)^2}{pq})$, this gives:
\[\text{obs}_g^{W_3}(p,q) = 2\left(1 - \frac{12(p-q)^2}{pq}\right) \cdot 
\left(\frac{\lambda_g^{(T)}}{2} + \frac{\lambda_g^{(W)}}{3}\right)\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}

\emph{Step 1: $W_3$ structure.}

The $W_3$ algebra has OPEs (Definition~\ref{def:w3-modes}):
\begin{align}
T(z)T(w) &\sim \frac{c/2}{(z-w)^4} + \cdots \\
W(z)W(w) &\sim \frac{c/3}{(z-w)^6} + \cdots
\end{align}

\emph{Step 2: Genus-$g$ differential.}

The bar differential at genus $g$ involves:
\begin{align}
d_g(T) &= \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} T \otimes T \otimes \omega_g^{(2)} \\
d_g(W) &= \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} W \otimes W \otimes \omega_g^{(3)}
\end{align}
where $\omega_g^{(h)}$ is the genus-$g$ form for weight-$h$ fields.

\emph{Step 3: Squaring the fiberwise differential and extracting obstruction.}

Compute $\dfib^{\,2}$:
\begin{align}
\dfib^{\,2}(T) &= \frac{c}{2} \cdot T \otimes \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} (\omega_g^{(2)})^2
= \frac{c}{2} \cdot T \otimes \lambda_g^{(2)} \\
\dfib^{\,2}(W) &= \frac{c}{3} \cdot W \otimes \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} (\omega_g^{(3)})^2
= \frac{c}{3} \cdot W \otimes \lambda_g^{(3)}
\end{align}

\emph{Step 4: Cross-terms vanish.}

The mixed terms $d_g^{(T)} d_g^{(W)} + d_g^{(W)} d_g^{(T)}$ involve the
$T$--$W$ OPE: $T(z)W(w) \sim 3W(w)/(z-w)^2 + \partial W(w)/(z-w)$.
Since this OPE has no central term (no $(z-w)^{-h}$ pole with $h \geq 4$
producing a scalar), the cross-term yields a coboundary
$d_g^{(T)} d_g^{(W)} + d_g^{(W)} d_g^{(T)} = 0$ in $H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$:
the residue extracts the zero-mode $T_0(W) = 3W$ (since $W$ is a Virasoro primary of weight~$3$
for the stress tensor~$T$), which is a field rather than a scalar,
and therefore vanishes in $H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ by the projection to the vacuum sector.

\emph{Step 5: Combined obstruction.}

The total obstruction is the sum of contributions from both generators:
\[\text{obs}_g^{W_3} = \frac{c}{2} \lambda_g^{(2)} + \frac{c}{3} \lambda_g^{(3)}\]
where $\lambda_g^{(j)} := c_g(R^0\pi_* \omega_{\mathcal{C}/\mathcal{M}_g}^{\otimes j})$ is the top Chern class of the bundle of $j$-differentials over $\mathcal{M}_g$.

\emph{Step 6: Arakawa verification.}

This formula matches Arakawa's results~\cite{Arakawa17} for W-algebras when
specialized to minimal models.
\end{proof}

\begin{computation}[Explicit genus-\texorpdfstring{$1$}{1} value of the \texorpdfstring{$W_3$}{W3} obstruction; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{comp:w3-obs-explicit}

For the $W_3$ minimal model $(p,q) = (5,4)$ with $c = \frac{4}{5}$:
\begin{align}
\text{obs}_1 &= \frac{4}{5} \cdot \left(\frac{\lambda_1^{(2)}}{2} +
\frac{\lambda_1^{(3)}}{3}\right)
\end{align}
By the Mumford isomorphism, the first Chern class of the bundle of $j$-differentials satisfies $c_1(\pi_* \omega^{\otimes j}) = (6j^2 - 6j + 1)\lambda_1$ on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}$.  Thus $\lambda_1^{(2)} = 13\lambda_1 = \frac{13}{24}$ and $\lambda_1^{(3)} = 37\lambda_1 = \frac{37}{24}$, giving:
\begin{align}
\text{obs}_1 &= \frac{4}{5} \cdot \left(\frac{13}{48} + \frac{37}{72}\right)
= \frac{4}{5} \cdot \frac{39 + 74}{144}
= \frac{4}{5} \cdot \frac{113}{144}
= \frac{113}{180}
\end{align}

For $g \geq 2$, the structural formula $\operatorname{obs}_g^{W_3} = (c/2)\lambda_g^{(2)} + (c/3)\lambda_g^{(3)}$ remains valid, but explicit numerical evaluation of $\lambda_g^{(j)} = c_g(\pi_* \omega^{\otimes j})$ requires Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ and is deferred.
\end{computation}

\subsection{Verification: obstruction squares to zero}
\label{subsec:obstruction-squares-zero}

\begin{theorem}[Nilpotence of obstruction (\texorpdfstring{$g \leq 2$}{g <= 2}); \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:obstruction-nilpotent}
For any augmented chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ and genus $g \leq 2$, the genus-$g$ obstruction satisfies:
\begin{equation}
(\text{obs}_g)^2 = 0 \quad \text{in } H^4(\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A}), Z(\mathcal{A}))
\end{equation}

This is a consistency condition ensuring the curved $A_\infty$ structure is well-defined.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For $g \leq 2$, nilpotence follows from dimensional vanishing.
By Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, $\operatorname{obs}_g$ is
proportional to the Hodge class $\lambda_g$, which lies in
$H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathbb{Q})$
(Table~\ref{tab:obstruction-summary}).  The cup product
$(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2$ therefore lies in
$H^{4g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A})^{\otimes 2})$.
Since $\dim_{\mathbb{R}} \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g = 6g - 6$, this
cohomology group vanishes whenever $4g > 6g - 6$, i.e., when
$g < 3$.
Case by case:
$g = 0$: $\operatorname{obs}_0 = 0$ by convention (the genus-$0$ bar complex has no curvature), so $(\operatorname{obs}_0)^2 = 0$;
$g = 1$: $(\operatorname{obs}_1)^2 \in H^4(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_1)$,
but $\dim_{\mathbb{R}} \overline{\mathcal{M}}_1 = 2$, so $H^4 = 0$;
$g = 2$: $(\operatorname{obs}_2)^2 \in H^8(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2)$,
but $\dim_{\mathbb{R}} \overline{\mathcal{M}}_2 = 6$, so $H^8 = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Nilpotence of obstruction (all genera); \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:obstruction-nilpotent-all-genera}
\label{thm:obstruction-nilpotent-higher}% backward-compatible label
\index{obstruction class!nilpotence!all genera}
For any Koszul chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ \emph{with a single strong
generator} and \emph{any} genus $g \geq 0$,
the genus-$g$ obstruction satisfies:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:obs-squared-zero-all-genera}
(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2 = 0 \quad \text{in }
H^{4g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A})^{\otimes 2}).
\end{equation}
For multi-generator algebras, see
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:multi-generator-nilpotence}} below.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality} (single strong generator hypothesis),
$\operatorname{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ where
$\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E}) \in \mathrm{CH}^g(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$
is the top Chern class of the rank-$g$ Hodge bundle~$\mathbb{E}$.
Therefore $(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2 = \kappa^2 \cdot \lambda_g^2$,
and it suffices to show $\lambda_g^2 = 0$ in
$\mathrm{CH}^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.

This is an immediate consequence of
\emph{Mumford's relation}~\cite{Mumford83}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mumford-relation}
c(\mathbb{E}) \cdot c(\mathbb{E}^\vee) = 1
\qquad \text{in } \mathrm{CH}^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g).
\end{equation}
Since $c_j(\mathbb{E}^\vee) = (-1)^j \lambda_j$ and
$\lambda_k = 0$ for $k > g$ (the Hodge bundle has rank~$g$),
extracting the degree-$2g$ component
of~\eqref{eq:mumford-relation} gives:
\[
\sum_{\substack{i + j = 2g \\ 0 \leq i,j \leq g}}
(-1)^j \lambda_i \lambda_j = 0.
\]
The only pair $(i,j)$ with $i + j = 2g$ and $0 \leq i,j \leq g$
is $i = j = g$.  The sum reduces to a single term:
\[
(-1)^g \lambda_g^2 = 0,
\]
whence $\lambda_g^2 = 0$ in
$\mathrm{CH}^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ for all $g \geq 1$.

\emph{Mumford's relation.}  The Gauss--Manin connection on the
de~Rham cohomology sheaf
\[
\mathcal{H}^1_{\mathrm{dR}}
= R^1\pi_*\Omega^{\bullet}_{\mathcal{C}/\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g}(\log D)
\]
is flat, so
$c(\mathcal{H}^1_{\mathrm{dR}}) = 1$.
The Hodge filtration gives an exact sequence
$0 \to \mathbb{E} \to \mathcal{H}^1_{\mathrm{dR}}
\to \mathbb{E}^\vee \to 0$, whence
$c(\mathbb{E}) \cdot c(\mathbb{E}^\vee)
= c(\mathcal{H}^1_{\mathrm{dR}}) = 1$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Comparison with the dimensional argument]
\label{rem:mumford-vs-dimension}
For $g \leq 2$, Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:obstruction-nilpotent}}
established $\lambda_g^2 = 0$ by the weaker observation that
$\mathrm{CH}^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g) = 0$ when
$2g > 3g - 3$, i.e., $g < 3$.
Mumford's relation is strictly stronger: it proves
$\lambda_g^2 = 0$ for \emph{all} genera, including $g = 3$
(where $\lambda_3^2 \in \mathrm{CH}^6(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_3)$
with $\dim \overline{\mathcal{M}}_3 = 6$, so the dimensional
argument fails) and all $g \geq 4$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Multi-generator nilpotence]\label{rem:multi-generator-nilpotence}
\index{obstruction class!nilpotence!multi-generator}
For multi-generator algebras, $\operatorname{obs}_g=\sum_i\kappa_{h_i}
\cdot\lambda_g^{(h_i)}$ with
$\lambda_g^{(j)}=c_g(R^0\pi_*\omega_X^{\otimes j})$.
Mumford's relation applies only to $j=1$; for $j\geq 2$ there is
no analogue.  Nilpotence $(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2=0$ holds for
$g\leq 2$ by dimension; for $g\geq 3$ and multi-generator
$\mathcal{W}_N$ it is open.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Mumford multiplicative relations for obstruction classes; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:mumford-multiplicative}
\index{Mumford relation!multiplicative consequences}
\index{obstruction class!multiplicative relations}
\index{lambda class@$\lambda$-class!product identities}
Let $\mathcal{A}$ be a Koszul chiral algebra with a single strong generator.
The obstruction classes
$\operatorname{obs}_g = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) \cdot \lambda_g$ satisfy the
following \emph{multiplicative relations}, inherited from
Mumford's relation~\eqref{eq:mumford-relation}:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \textbf{Nilpotence} (Theorem~\ref{thm:obstruction-nilpotent-all-genera}):
$(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2 = 0$ for all $g \geq 1$.
\item \textbf{Degree-$k$ Mumford relations}: For each
$k = 1, \ldots, 2g$,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:mumford-degree-k}
\sum_{\substack{i + j = k \\ 0 \leq i,j \leq g}}
(-1)^j \operatorname{obs}_i \cdot \operatorname{obs}_j = 0
\qquad \text{in } \mathrm{CH}^k(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g) \otimes Z(\mathcal{A})^{\otimes 2}.
\end{equation}
\item \textbf{Recursive structure}: Setting $k = 2$ in~\eqref{eq:mumford-degree-k}
gives $(\operatorname{obs}_1)^2 = 2 \operatorname{obs}_2$. More generally, for $g \geq 3$,
setting $k = 2g - 2$ gives the recurrence:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:lambda-recurrence}
\lambda_{g-1}^2 = 2\lambda_g \cdot \lambda_{g-2}
\qquad \text{in } \mathrm{CH}^{2g-2}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g).
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Since $\operatorname{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ by
Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, part~(b) follows from extracting
the degree-$k$ component of Mumford's relation
$c(\mathbb{E}) \cdot c(\mathbb{E}^\vee) = 1$, then scaling by
$\kappa^2$.  Part~(a) is the case $k = 2g$.

For part~(c), the degree-$2$ relation reads
$\lambda_2 - \lambda_1^2 + \lambda_2 = 0$, i.e.,
$\lambda_1^2 = 2\lambda_2$.  For the degree-$(2g-2)$ relation with
$g \geq 3$, the constraint $0 \leq i,j \leq g$ with $i + j = 2g - 2$
admits three pairs: $(g, g-2)$, $(g-1, g-1)$, $(g-2, g)$.
The relation becomes
\[
(-1)^{g-2}\lambda_g \lambda_{g-2}
+ (-1)^{g-1}\lambda_{g-1}^2
+ (-1)^{g}\lambda_{g-2}\lambda_g = 0.
\]
Since $\lambda_i \lambda_j = \lambda_j \lambda_i$ in
$\mathrm{CH}^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$, factoring
$(-1)^{g-2}$ yields
$2\lambda_g \lambda_{g-2} - \lambda_{g-1}^2 = 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Chern character reformulation]
\label{rem:chern-character-mumford}
Mumford's relation $c(\mathbb{E}) \cdot c(\mathbb{E}^\vee) = 1$
is equivalent to $\operatorname{ch}(\mathbb{E} \oplus \mathbb{E}^\vee)$ being
concentrated in degree~$0$, since $\mathbb{E} \oplus \mathbb{E}^\vee
= \mathcal{H}^1_{\mathrm{dR}}$ has trivial Chern character.
Via the Newton identities relating power sums to elementary symmetric
functions, all $\lambda$-class products are determined by the
Bernoulli-number weighted traces
$\operatorname{ch}_k(\mathbb{E}) = B_k \cdot \kappa_k / k!$
(where $\kappa_k$ are the Miller--Morita--Mumford classes),
giving the full multiplicative structure of the obstruction ring.
\end{remark}

\begin{example}[Heisenberg case]\label{ex:heisenberg-obs-squares}
For the Heisenberg algebra with
$\operatorname{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$,
Theorem~\ref{thm:obstruction-nilpotent-all-genera} gives
$(\operatorname{obs}_g)^2 = \kappa^2 \cdot \lambda_g^2 = 0$
for \emph{all} $g \geq 1$, by Mumford's relation.
\end{example}

\subsection{Summary table: obstruction classes for key examples}
\label{subsec:obstruction-summary-table}

\begin{table}[ht]
\centering
\caption{Genus-$g$ obstruction classes}
\label{tab:obstruction-summary}
\begin{tabular}{|l|c|c|}
\hline
\textbf{Chiral Algebra} & \textbf{Obstruction $\text{obs}_g$} & \textbf{Physical Meaning} \\
\hline
Heisenberg $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ & $\kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ & Level shift / central charge \\
\hline
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_2(k)$ & $\frac{3(k+2)}{4} \lambda_g$ & Affine level shift \\
\hline
$\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_3(k)$ & $\frac{4(k+3)}{3} \lambda_g$ & Affine level shift \\
\hline
$\widehat{E_8}(k)$ & $\frac{62(k+30)}{15} \lambda_g$ & Affine level shift \\
\hline
$W_3(c)$ & $c \cdot (\frac{\lambda_g^{(T)}}{2} + \frac{\lambda_g^{(W)}}{3})$ & 
Conformal anomaly \\
\hline
Virasoro $(c)$ & $\frac{c}{2} \lambda_g$ & Conformal anomaly \\
\hline
\end{tabular}
\end{table}

\begin{theorem}[Genus universality; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:genus-universality}
\index{genus universality theorem|textbf}
\textup{[Regime: curved-central on the Koszul locus; all genera
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

The Heisenberg factorization $\mathrm{obs}_g = k \cdot \lambda_g$ (\S\ref{sec:frame-genus-tower}) is universal.

For every Koszul chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ with a single strong generator, there is a genus-independent scalar $\kappa(\mathcal{A})$, determined by the genus-$1$ curvature, such that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:genus-universality}
\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) \;=\; \kappa(\mathcal{A}) \cdot \lambda_g
\qquad \text{in } H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g),
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E})$ is the top Chern class of the Hodge bundle.

For algebras with generators of several conformal weights, the
cohomological obstruction may split into several Hodge-type pieces; the
universal scalar statement is then the free-energy formula in
\textup{(iii)} together with
Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:multi-generator-obs}}.

\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{(i)}] \emph{Explicit values.}
$\kappa(\mathcal{H}_\kappa) = \kappa$,\;
$\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k) = \frac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\mathfrak{g}}{2h^\vee}$,\;
$\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = \frac{c}{2}$.
\item[\textup{(ii)}] \emph{Duality.}
For affine Kac--Moody algebras $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ with Feigin--Frenkel dual
$\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{-k-2h^\vee}$: $\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = -\kappa(\mathcal{A})$.
For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras $\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}, f_{\mathrm{prin}})$ obtained by Drinfeld--Sokolov
reduction: $\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = \varrho(\mathfrak{g})\, K - \kappa(\mathcal{A})$, where
$K = c(\mathcal{A}) + c(\mathcal{A}^!)$ is the complementarity constant
(Remark~\ref{rem:vir-vs-km-complementarity}) and
$\varrho(\mathfrak{g}) = \sum_{i=1}^r \frac{1}{m_i + 1}$ is the exponent sum
($m_1, \ldots, m_r$ the exponents of~$\mathfrak{g}$; for $\mathcal{W}_N = \mathcal{W}(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$,
$\varrho = H_N - 1 = \sum_{s=2}^{N} 1/s$).
In particular, $\kappa + \kappa' = 0$ for Kac--Moody,
$\kappa + \kappa' = 13$ for the Virasoro algebra ($\varrho = 1/2$, $K = 26$),
and $\kappa + \kappa' = 250/3$ for $\mathcal{W}_3$ ($\varrho = 5/6$, $K = 100$).
The obstruction coefficient $\kappa = 0$ if and only if $\mathcal{A}$ is at critical level;
for Kac--Moody the dual is then also critical, but for $\mathcal{W}$-algebras
$\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = \varrho(\mathfrak{g})\, K \neq 0$.

\emph{Abelian case.}
The Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ is the abelian Kac--Moody algebra
($\mathfrak{g}$ abelian, $h^\vee = 0$).  The general formula
$\kappa = (k + h^\vee)\dim\mathfrak{g}/(2h^\vee)$ has a removable singularity
at $h^\vee = 0$; one defines $\kappa(\mathcal{H}_\kappa) = \kappa$ directly
from the genus-$1$ curvature (Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs}).
The duality $\kappa + \kappa' = 0$ still holds: $\kappa(\mathcal{H}_\kappa^!) = -\kappa$,
consistent with the Koszul dual $\mathrm{Sym}^{\mathrm{ch}}(V^*)$ being curved with
curvature $m_0 = -\kappa$.  The complementarity constant $c + c'$ is not defined
in the usual sense because the dual is a curved (non-conformal) chiral algebra.
\item[\textup{(iii)}] \emph{Faber--Pandharipande formula.}
The genus-$g$ free energy is
$F_g = \kappa \cdot \frac{2^{2g-1}-1}{2^{2g-1}} \cdot \frac{|B_{2g}|}{(2g)!}$,
where $B_{2g}$ are Bernoulli numbers.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The factorization \eqref{eq:genus-universality} follows from the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs}:
the propagator $\omega_g$ on the genus-$g$ surface acquires a $B$-cycle defect
equal to $\lambda_g$, and the algebra-specific contribution collapses to
the genus-$1$ curvature coefficient $\kappa(\mathcal{A})$.
For algebras with generators of uniform conformal weight~$h$, the
factorization is immediate and $\kappa$ is a single scalar.
The reason is that the fiberwise curvature coderivation
$\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa \cdot \omega_g$ acts on the space of generators~$V$;
when all generators have weight~$h$, the Hodge bundle contributes
$h \cdot \lambda_g$ on each generator, so the total curvature is
$\kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ with $\kappa$ a \emph{scalar}.
When generators have different weights $h_1, \ldots, h_r$, the curvature
is instead a diagonal matrix $\operatorname{diag}(\kappa_{h_1}, \ldots,
\kappa_{h_r})$ tensored with weight-dependent Hodge classes---a
\emph{matrix-valued} class on~$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.
(Uniform weight holds for single-generator algebras such as
Heisenberg and Virasoro, and also for Kac--Moody algebras where all
currents $J^a$ have weight~$1$; it excludes $\mathcal{W}$-algebras
with generators of different weights.)
For algebras with multiple generators of different conformal weights
(e.g.\ $\mathcal{W}_3$ with generators of weights~$2$ and~$3$),
the genus-$g$ obstruction is \emph{a priori} a sum
$\mathrm{obs}_g = \sum_j \kappa_j \cdot \lambda_g^{(j)}$
where $\lambda_g^{(j)} = c_g(R^0\pi_* \omega_X^j)$.
At genus~$1$, all Hodge-type classes are proportional to $\lambda_1$
(since $H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}) \cong \mathbb{C}$), and
$\kappa = \sum_j \kappa_j$ is the total obstruction coefficient.
At genus $g \geq 2$ the individual $\lambda_g^{(j)}$ may differ;
the universality formula $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$
holds at the level of \emph{free energies}
$F_g = \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} \mathrm{obs}_g$
via the Faber--Pandharipande formula, which evaluates each
$\lambda_g^{(j)}$ against $\psi$-classes.
Part (i) follows from the explicit genus-$1$ computations
(Heisenberg: Theorem~\ref{thm:heisenberg-obs};
Kac--Moody: Theorem~\ref{thm:kac-moody-obs};
Virasoro: Theorem~\ref{thm:vir-genus1-curvature}).
Part (ii): for Kac--Moody, $\kappa = \frac{(k+h^\vee)\dim\mathfrak{g}}{2h^\vee}$
is linear in the shifted level $t = k + h^\vee$; the Feigin--Frenkel involution
$t \mapsto -t$ gives $\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = -\kappa(\mathcal{A})$.
For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras, $\kappa = c \cdot \varrho(\mathfrak{g})$ where
$\varrho(\mathfrak{g}) = \sum 1/(m_i+1)$ is the exponent sum
(Theorem~\ref{thm:wn-obstruction}).  Since $c \mapsto c' = K - c$
under the Feigin--Frenkel involution,
$\kappa' = c' \cdot \varrho = (K-c)\varrho = \varrho K - \kappa$
(see the explicit verifications in \S\ref{sec:genus-all-master}).
Part (iii) is the Faber--Pandharipande evaluation
$\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}} \psi_1^{2g-2}\,\lambda_g = \frac{2^{2g-1}-1}{2^{2g-1}} \cdot \frac{|B_{2g}|}{(2g)!}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mumford-formula}).
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Multi-generator obstruction]\label{rem:multi-generator-obs}
For an algebra with generators of conformal weights $h_1, \ldots, h_r$,
the genus-$g$ obstruction is \emph{a priori}
$\mathrm{obs}_g = \sum_{i=1}^r \kappa_{h_i} \lambda_g^{(h_i)}$,
where $\lambda_g^{(j)} = c_g(R^0\pi_*\omega^{\otimes j})$.
At genus~$1$ all $\lambda_1^{(j)}$ are proportional to $\lambda_1$
(since $H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}) \cong \mathbb{C}$),
so the total reduces to a single scalar $\kappa = \sum_i \kappa_{h_i}$.
At genus $g \geq 2$ the individual Hodge-type classes $\lambda_g^{(j)}$
need not be proportional in $H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.
Nevertheless, the Faber--Pandharipande formula evaluates each
$\lambda_g^{(j)}$ against $\psi$-classes to the same Bernoulli expression,
so universality holds at the level of free energies.
Whether \eqref{eq:genus-universality} holds as a \emph{cohomological} identity
for multi-generator algebras remains open.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Multi-generator obstruction decomposition; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:multi-generator-obstruction}
\index{multi-generator obstruction}
Let $\cA$ be a modular Koszul chiral algebra with strong generators
of conformal weights $h_1, \ldots, h_r$.
Then the genus-$g$ obstruction decomposes as
\begin{equation}\label{eq:multi-generator-decomp}
\mathrm{obs}_g(\cA) \;=\;
\sum_{i=1}^{r} \kappa_{h_i}(\cA) \cdot \lambda_g^{(h_i)}
\qquad \text{in } H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g),
\end{equation}
where $\lambda_g^{(j)} = c_g(R^0\pi_*\omega^{\otimes j})$ and
$\kappa_{h_i}(\cA)$ is the partial modular characteristic at
weight~$h_i$, determined by the genus-$1$ curvature of the
weight-$h_i$ sector.  At genus~$1$,
$\mathrm{obs}_1(\cA) = \kappa(\cA) \cdot \lambda_1$
with $\kappa(\cA) = \sum_{i=1}^r \kappa_{h_i}(\cA)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The fiber differential decomposes by conformal weight into
independent bar complexes for each generator: the weight-$h_i$
sector contributes its own curvature $\kappa_{h_i}$, and the
genus-$g$ obstruction is the sum of the fiberwise Euler classes.
The Hodge-type bundle $\mathbb{E}_j = R^0\pi_*\omega^{\otimes j}$
has rank $(2j-1)(g-1)$ for $j \geq 2$, and its top Chern class
$\lambda_g^{(j)}$ provides the characteristic class.
At genus~$1$, $H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1}) \cong \mathbb{C}$
forces all $\lambda_1^{(j)}$ to be proportional to~$\lambda_1$,
reducing the sum to the single scalar
$\kappa(\cA) = \sum_i \kappa_{h_i}(\cA)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Anomaly ratio identity; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:anomaly-ratio}
\index{anomaly ratio|textbf}
For any $\mathcal{W}$-algebra $\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g})$, the obstruction coefficient $\kappa$ and central charge $c$ are related by
\begin{equation}\label{eq:anomaly-ratio}
\frac{\kappa(\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}))}{c(\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}))} = \varrho(\mathfrak{g}) := \sum_{i=1}^r \frac{1}{m_i + 1}
\end{equation}
where $m_1, \ldots, m_r$ are the exponents of $\mathfrak{g}$.  The ratio $\varrho(\mathfrak{g})$ is a root-system invariant independent of the level~$k$.

For Kac--Moody algebras $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$ (before DS reduction), $\kappa/c = (k+h^\vee)^2/(2h^\vee k)$, which depends on the level.  The level-independence of $\kappa/c$ is specific to $\mathcal{W}$-algebras and reflects the DS reduction.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
From Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}(ii): $\kappa = c \cdot \varrho(\mathfrak{g})$.  Since $\varrho$ depends only on the exponents of $\mathfrak{g}$, it is independent of $k$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[\texorpdfstring{$\kappa$}{kappa}-periodicity under level shift; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:kappa-periodicity}
\index{obstruction coefficient!periodicity}
For affine Kac--Moody $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$, the obstruction coefficient is periodic under level shift: $\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{k+n}) = \kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k) + n \cdot d/(2h^\vee)$ for $n \in \mathbb{Z}$.  In particular, the free energy $F_g$ is a linear function of $k$ with slope $\lambda_g^{FP} \cdot d/(2h^\vee)$.  For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras, $\kappa$ is a rational function of $k$ (through its dependence on the DS central charge), and the periodicity statement becomes: $\kappa(\mathcal{W}^{k+n}(\mathfrak{g})) - \kappa(\mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{g}))$ is a rational function of $k$ with poles only at $k = -h^\vee$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
For KM: $\kappa = (k+h^\vee)d/(2h^\vee)$, which is linear in $k$ with slope $d/(2h^\vee)$.  Level shift $k \to k+n$ adds $nd/(2h^\vee)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Universality principle]\label{rem:lambda-universality}
The factorization $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ holds at the cohomology-class level for single-generator algebras (Heisenberg, Virasoro, Kac--Moody).  For multi-generator algebras such as $\mathcal{W}_3$,
the obstruction is $\mathrm{obs}_g = (c/2)\,\lambda_g^{(T)} + (c/3)\,\lambda_g^{(W)}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:w3-obstruction}), with contributions proportional at genus~$1$ but possibly distinct at $g \geq 2$.
Universality~\eqref{eq:genus-universality} and the free energy formula~(iii) hold at the level of integrated invariants $F_g = \int \mathrm{obs}_g$, where all $\lambda$-class contributions collapse to a single Faber--Pandharipande evaluation.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Additivity of the obstruction coefficient; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{cor:kappa-additivity}
\index{obstruction coefficient!additivity}
For Koszul chiral algebras $\mathcal{A}$, $\mathcal{B}$ such that $\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}$ is Koszul:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:kappa-additivity}
\kappa(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) + \kappa(\mathcal{B}).
\end{equation}
In particular, $\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = \mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) + \mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{B})$ for all $g \geq 1$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The singular part of the OPE of $\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}$ is the sum of the singular parts of $\mathcal{A}$ and $\mathcal{B}$ (the tensor product acts on disjoint sets of fields).  The genus-$1$ curvature, which determines $\kappa$ by Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, is therefore additive.  Since the Faber--Pandharipande integral $\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$ is linear in $\kappa$, the factorization~\eqref{eq:genus-universality} gives $\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = (\kappa(\mathcal{A}) + \kappa(\mathcal{B})) \cdot \lambda_g = \mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) + \mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{B})$.
\end{proof}

\begin{example}
For a rank-$d$ lattice vertex algebra $V_\Lambda = \mathcal{H}_1^{\otimes d}$, additivity gives $\kappa(V_\Lambda) = d \cdot \kappa(\mathcal{H}_1) = d$, confirming the Master Table entry (Table~\ref{tab:master-invariants}).  For the $bc$--$\beta\gamma$ system, $\kappa(bc \otimes \beta\gamma) = c/2 + (-c/2) = 0$ (since $\kappa(\beta\gamma) = -\kappa(bc)$ by Theorem~\ref{thm:fermion-all-genera}).
\end{example}

\begin{corollary}[Obstruction complementarity for \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal{W}_N$}{W(N)}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{cor:kappa-sum-wn}
\index{obstruction coefficient!W-algebra complementarity}
For the principal $\mathcal{W}$-algebra $\mathcal{W}_N = \mathcal{W}^k(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$, the obstruction complementarity sum is
\begin{equation}\label{eq:kappa-sum-wn}
\kappa(\mathcal{W}_N^k) + \kappa(\mathcal{W}_N^{k'}) = (H_N - 1) \cdot K_N
\end{equation}
where $H_N = \sum_{s=1}^N 1/s$ is the $N$-th harmonic number, $K_N = c + c' = 2(N-1)(2N^2+2N+1)$ is the Koszul conductor, and $k' = -k-2N$.  The first values are:
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{cccc}
$N$ & $\varrho = H_N - 1$ & $K_N$ & $\kappa + \kappa'$ \\
\hline
$2$ & $1/2$ & $26$ & $13$ \\
$3$ & $5/6$ & $100$ & $250/3$ \\
$4$ & $13/12$ & $246$ & $533/2$ \\
$5$ & $77/60$ & $488$ & $9394/15$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}(ii), $\kappa(\mathcal{W}_N^k) = c \cdot \varrho(\mathfrak{sl}_N)$ where $\varrho(\mathfrak{sl}_N) = \sum_{s=2}^N 1/s = H_N - 1$.  Under the Feigin--Frenkel involution $k \mapsto k' = -k - 2N$, $c \mapsto c' = K_N - c$, so $\kappa' = (K_N - c)(H_N - 1)$ and $\kappa + \kappa' = K_N(H_N - 1)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Critical level characterization; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{cor:critical-level-universality}
\index{critical level!characterization}
For a Koszul chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$, the following are equivalent:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $\kappa(\mathcal{A}) = 0$;
\item $\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) = 0$ for all $g \geq 1$;
\item $F_g(\mathcal{A}) = 0$ for all $g \geq 1$;
\item the bar complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})$ is uncurved \textup{(}$m_1^2 = 0$\textup{)};
\item $\mathcal{A}$ is at critical level: $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})) \simeq \mathcal{A}$ \textup{(}uncurved bar-cobar\textup{)}.
\end{enumerate}
Moreover, when these hold, $H^0(\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A}))$ is a genuine associative chiral algebra \textup{(}not merely $A_\infty$\textup{)}.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
(i)$\Rightarrow$(ii): By Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g = 0$.
(ii)$\Rightarrow$(iii): $F_g = \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}} \psi_1^{2g-2}\, \mathrm{obs}_g = 0$.
(iii)$\Rightarrow$(i): If $F_1 = \kappa/24 = 0$, then $\kappa = 0$.
(i)$\Leftrightarrow$(iv): The curvature $m_0 \propto \kappa$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:km-bar-curvature} for Kac--Moody; the general case follows from the genus-$1$ computation).  Thus $\kappa = 0$ iff $m_0 = 0$ iff $m_1^2 = 0$.
(iv)$\Rightarrow$(v): When uncurved, the bar-cobar adjunction (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-cobar-isomorphism-main}) is a genuine quasi-isomorphism.
The final assertion follows: with $m_1^2 = 0$, the bar complex is a strict dg coalgebra, so its cobar is a strict dg algebra, and $H^0$ inherits a strict associative product.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Tautological class map; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{cor:tautological-class-map}
\index{tautological ring!map from chiral algebras}
Every Koszul chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ determines a distinguished tautological class
\[
\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) \cdot \lambda_g \;\in\; R^g(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)
\]
in the tautological ring of the moduli space.  The assignment $\mathcal{A} \mapsto \kappa(\mathcal{A})$ is additive under tensor products: $\kappa(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) + \kappa(\mathcal{B})$ \textup{(}Corollary~\ref{cor:kappa-additivity}\textup{)}.  For Kac--Moody algebras, $\kappa$ further satisfies $\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = -\kappa(\mathcal{A})$, making it a group homomorphism from $K_0(\mathrm{KCA}_{\mathrm{KM}})$ to~$\mathbb{Q}$.  For $\mathcal{W}$-algebras the duality relation is affine \textup{(}$\kappa' = \varrho(\mathfrak{g})\,K - \kappa$, where $\varrho(\mathfrak{g}) = \sum 1/(m_i+1)$\textup{)}, so $\kappa$ is additive but does not intertwine Koszul duality with negation.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
That $\mathrm{obs}_g(\mathcal{A}) = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) \cdot \lambda_g$ lies in $R^g(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ follows from Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, since $\lambda_g$ is tautological.  Additivity $\kappa(\mathcal{A} \otimes \mathcal{B}) = \kappa(\mathcal{A}) + \kappa(\mathcal{B})$ (Corollary~\ref{cor:kappa-additivity}) gives a group homomorphism $K_0(\mathrm{KCA}) \to \mathbb{Q}$ with respect to tensor products.  For Kac--Moody families the additional relation $\kappa(\mathcal{A}^!) = -\kappa(\mathcal{A})$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}(ii)) shows that $\kappa$ also intertwines Koszul duality with negation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}\label{rem:tautological-master-table}
The Master Table of computed invariants (Table~\ref{tab:master-invariants}) gives explicit values: $\kappa(\mathcal{H}_1) = 1$, $\kappa(\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}}_{2,k}) = 3(k+2)/4$, $\kappa(\mathrm{Vir}_c) = c/2$, $\kappa(\mathcal{W}_N^k) = c \cdot (H_N - 1)$.  Each produces a one-parameter family of tautological classes $\kappa \cdot \lambda_g \in R^g(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.
These scalars are the trace of the universal MC class
$\Theta_{\cA}$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:explicit-theta}):
the appearance of $\kappa$ as a single controlling number
reflects the one-dimensionality of
$H^2_{\mathrm{cyc}}(\mathfrak{g},\mathfrak{g}) \cong \mathbb{C}$
for simple~$\mathfrak{g}$ --- there is only one direction for
$\Theta$ to point
(Corollary~\ref{cor:scalar-saturation}).
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Tautological span]\label{rem:tautological-span}
\index{tautological ring!span from Koszul algebras}
The collection $\{\kappa(\mathcal{A}) \cdot \lambda_g : \mathcal{A} \text{ Koszul}\}$ generates a rank-$1$ subgroup of $R^g(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$ for each $g$, since all obstruction classes are proportional to $\lambda_g$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}).  The image of the group homomorphism $K_0(\mathrm{KCA}) \to \mathbb{Q}$ (Corollary~\ref{cor:tautological-class-map}) is $\mathbb{Q}$ itself: the Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ achieves any rational $\kappa$, and additivity (Corollary~\ref{cor:kappa-additivity}) extends the range to all of~$\mathbb{Q}$.

A natural question is whether the \emph{full} bar complex $\bar{B}^{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathcal{A})$---not just its genus-$g$ cohomology class---provides higher tautological classes beyond $\lambda_g$.  The bar spectral sequence $E_r^{p,q} \Rightarrow H^{p+q}(\bar{B}^{(g)})$ has $E_2$ page involving products of $\psi$-classes and $\lambda$-classes on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$, which a priori lie in a larger part of $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.  However, the collapse at $E_2$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:spectral-sequence-collapse}) reduces all contributions to the single class $\kappa \cdot \lambda_g$, so no additional tautological classes emerge from the bar complex at the level of cohomology.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Bar spectral sequence and tautological filtration;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{prop:bar-tautological-filtration}
\index{tautological ring!bar spectral sequence filtration}
The bar spectral sequence
$E_r^{p,q} \Rightarrow H^{p+q}(\bar{B}^{(g)}(\mathcal{A}))$
induces a \emph{tautological filtration} on the bar cohomology:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:tauto-filtration}
0 = F^{3g-2} \subset F^{3g-3} \subset \cdots \subset F^0 =
H^*(\bar{B}^{(g)}(\mathcal{A}))
\end{equation}
where $F^p / F^{p+1} = E_\infty^{p,*}$.  The associated graded
pieces satisfy:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item $E_2^{p,q}$ involves classes in
  $H^p(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{H}^q(\bar{B}^{(g)}_\bullet))$,
  which lie in the tautological ring $R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$
  for Koszul algebras;
\item The differential $d_2\colon E_2^{p,q} \to E_2^{p+2,q-1}$
  is the Kodaira--Spencer map, which produces $\psi$-classes and
  boundary classes from $\lambda$-classes;
\item The differential $d_3$ involves triple Massey products,
  producing $\kappa$-classes from $\psi$-classes.
\end{enumerate}
For a Koszul algebra with the spectral sequence collapsing at
$E_2$, only $\lambda_g$ survives.  If the spectral sequence does
\emph{not} collapse at $E_2$, the higher differentials produce
additional tautological classes.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The filtration~\eqref{eq:tauto-filtration} is standard for any
spectral sequence converging to a graded group.  Part~(i): the
$E_2$ page is a Leray-type spectral sequence for the universal
curve over $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n}$
(Section~\ref{sec:genus-spectral-complete}), and for Koszul
algebras the local system $\mathcal{H}^q$ is a variation of Hodge
structure, placing the cohomology classes in $R^*$ by
\cite[Appendix~A]{FP00}.

Part~(ii): The differential $d_2$ is the Kodaira--Spencer map
\begin{multline*}
\mathrm{KS}\colon H^p(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, R^q\pi_*\mathcal{A}) \\
\to H^{p+2}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, R^{q-1}\pi_*\mathcal{A}),
\end{multline*}
which is a cup product with the Kodaira--Spencer class
$\mathrm{KS} \in H^1(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g,
T_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g})$.  This class is dual to
$\psi_1 \in H^1(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1})$ under the
cotangent-tangent pairing.  When $d_2$ acts on a $\lambda$-class,
the result involves $\psi$-classes and boundary divisor classes
$[\Delta_{\mathrm{irr}}]$, $[\Delta_{i,S}]$.

Part~(iii): The differential $d_3$ is a triple Massey product in
the $A_\infty$ structure (Theorem~\ref{thm:bar-ainfty-complete}).
On $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$, the Massey product
$\langle \psi_i, \psi_j, \psi_k \rangle$ produces
$\kappa$-classes $\kappa_m = \pi_*(\psi^{m+1})$ by the
push-forward formula.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Tautological classes beyond \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_g$}{lambda-g}]
\label{rem:tauto-beyond-lambda}
\index{tautological ring!beyond lambda classes}
The bar complex can produce tautological classes beyond $\lambda_g$
via two mechanisms: (1)~non-collapsing spectral sequences (no
current example among Master Table algebras); (2)~module insertions,
where $\mathrm{obs}_{g,n}=\kappa\cdot\lambda_g\cdot
\prod_i\psi_i^{h_i}$ gives products in
$R^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,n})$.
The second is implicit in the Verlinde formula.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Grothendieck group of Koszul chiral algebras; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:koszul-k0}
\index{Grothendieck group!Koszul chiral algebras}
Let $\mathrm{KCA}$ denote the category of Koszul chiral algebras with tensor product $\otimes$.  The obstruction coefficient defines a group homomorphism
\[
\kappa: K_0(\mathrm{KCA}, \otimes) \to (\mathbb{Q}, +)
\]
from the Grothendieck group to the rationals.  This homomorphism is:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{Surjective}: the Heisenberg family $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ achieves any $\kappa \in \mathbb{Q}$;
\item \emph{Non-injective}: the kernel contains all algebras at critical level ($\kappa = 0$);
\item \emph{Compatible with Koszul duality}: for Kac--Moody algebras, $\kappa(\cA^!) = -\kappa(\cA)$, so the Koszul involution acts as negation on the image.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Additivity is Corollary~\ref{cor:kappa-additivity}.  The unit $\mathbf{1}$ (trivial algebra) has $\kappa(\mathbf{1}) = 0$.  Surjectivity follows from $\kappa(\mathcal{H}_q) = q$ for $q \in \mathbb{Q}$.  Non-injectivity: the Feigin--Frenkel center $\mathfrak{z}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{-h^\vee})$ is a non-trivial Koszul algebra with $\kappa = 0$.  Part (iii) is Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}(ii).
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Uncurved quotient]\label{def:uncurved-quotient}
\index{uncurved quotient category}
The \emph{uncurved quotient} of the category $\mathrm{KCA}$ is the localization
\[
\mathrm{KCA}^{\mathrm{unc}} := \mathrm{KCA}[\kappa^{-1}(0)]
\]
at the full subcategory of algebras with $\kappa = 0$.  Objects of $\mathrm{KCA}^{\mathrm{unc}}$ are equivalence classes of Koszul chiral algebras modulo critical-level algebras: $\cA \sim \mathcal{B}$ if $\cA \otimes \mathcal{C} \simeq \mathcal{B} \otimes \mathcal{C}'$ for some $\mathcal{C}, \mathcal{C}'$ with $\kappa = 0$.  By Theorem~\ref{thm:koszul-k0}, the obstruction coefficient $\kappa$ is a complete invariant on $K_0(\mathrm{KCA}^{\mathrm{unc}})$.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Connection to deformation-obstruction complementarity}
\label{subsec:obstruction-deformation-connection}

\begin{theorem}[Obstruction-deformation pairing; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]\label{thm:obs-def-pairing-explicit}
\textup{[Regime: curved-central on the Koszul locus; all genera
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})}.]}

\leavevmode\\
The obstruction class
$\text{obs}_g \in H^2(\bar{B}_g(\mathcal{A}), Z(\mathcal{A}))$
pairs with the deformation space $Q_g(\mathcal{A}^!)$ via
\begin{equation}
\langle \text{obs}_g, \text{def}_g \rangle = \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} 
\text{obs}_g \wedge \text{def}_g
\end{equation}

This pairing is perfect, giving:
\[Q_g(\mathcal{A}) \oplus Q_g(\mathcal{A}^!) \cong H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, 
Z(\mathcal{A}))\]
as stated in Theorem~\ref{thm:deformation-obstruction}.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Proof via Serre duality]

\emph{Step 1: Serre duality on moduli space.}

By Serre duality on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$:
\[H^i(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A}))^* \cong 
H^{3g-3-i}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A}^!) \otimes \omega_{\mathcal{M}_g})\]

\emph{Step 2: Obstructions vs deformations.}

Obstructions and deformations live in complementary degrees determined
by $\mathcal{A}$:
\begin{align}
\text{obs}_g &\in H^i(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A})) \\
\text{def}_g &\in H^{3g-3-i}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A}^!))
\end{align}
where the degree $i$ depends on the chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$
(for the Heisenberg at level $\kappa$: $i = 2g$;
in general $i$ is determined by the cohomological degree of
the leading obstruction class)

\emph{Step 3: Pairing via integration.}

The pairing is:
\[\langle \text{obs}_g, \text{def}_g \rangle = \int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g} 
\text{obs}_g \cup \text{def}_g \in \mathbb{C}\]

This is well-defined because:
\[i + (3g-3-i) = 3g-3 = \dim_{\mathbb{C}}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)\]

\emph{Step 4: Non-degeneracy.}

The pairing is non-degenerate by Poincaré duality on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.

Therefore, obstructions and deformations are mutually dual.
\end{proof}

\begin{example}[Heisenberg pairing]\label{ex:heisenberg-pairing}
For the Heisenberg algebra $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$:
\begin{align}
\text{obs}_g &= \kappa \cdot \lambda_g \in H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g) \\
\text{def}_g &\in H^{4g-6}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)
\end{align}

The degrees are complementary under Poincar\'e duality: $\dim_{\mathbb{R}}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g) = 6g - 6$, so $H^{2g}$ pairs with $H^{6g-6-2g} = H^{4g-6}$.

\emph{Note:} The deformation degree is $4g - 6$.
At $g = 1$, $4g - 6 = -2 < 0$, so $\text{def}_1 = 0$:
the genus-$1$ obstruction is uncompensated.
At $g = 2$, $\text{def}_2 \in H^2(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_2)$
(a $3$-dimensional space).
At $g = 3$, $\text{def}_3 \in H^6(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_3) = H^{\mathrm{top}} \cong \mathbb{C}$, so the deformation is a scalar.
For $g \geq 2$, the Poincar\'e duality pairing couples
$\text{obs}_g$ with $\text{def}_g$:
\begin{align}
\langle \text{obs}_g, \text{def}_g \rangle &= \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} (\kappa \cdot \lambda_g)
\cup (\kappa^{-1} \cdot \lambda_{g-3}^*) \\
&= \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} \lambda_g \cup \lambda_{g-3}^* \quad (g \geq 4)
\end{align}
\end{example}

\begin{remark}[Hodge filtration compatibility]\label{rem:hodge-filtration}
\index{Hodge filtration!bar complex}
The genus universality factorization $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}) is compatible with the Hodge filtration on $H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$.  Since $\lambda_g = c_g(\mathbb{E})$ is a Hodge class of type $(g,g)$ in $H^{2g}(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$, the obstruction $\mathrm{obs}_g(\cA)$ lies in the middle Hodge piece $F^g H^{2g} \cap \overline{F}^g H^{2g}$.  This constrains the deformation space $Q_g(\cA^!)$ (Theorem~\ref{thm:obs-def-pairing-explicit}) to have a complementary Hodge type.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Obstruction lifting criterion; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:obstruction-lifting}
\index{obstruction!lifting criterion}
A Koszul chiral algebra $\cA$ at genus $g$ lifts to genus $g+1$ (i.e., $\mathrm{obs}_{g+1}(\cA) = 0$ in the appropriate obstruction group) if and only if $\kappa(\cA) = 0$.  Equivalently:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item If $\kappa \neq 0$, the bar complex has nontrivial curvature at \emph{every} genus $g \geq 1$;
\item If $\kappa = 0$, the bar complex is uncurved at \emph{all} genera simultaneously.
\end{enumerate}
There is no intermediate case: the genus-$1$ obstruction determines all higher-genus obstructions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality}, $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$ with $\lambda_g \neq 0$ for all $g \geq 1$ (the Hodge class is nonzero).  Thus $\mathrm{obs}_g = 0$ for some $g$ iff $\kappa = 0$ iff $\mathrm{obs}_g = 0$ for all $g$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Dichotomy from the universal class]
\label{rem:dichotomy-theta}
The $0/\infty$ dichotomy is geometric:
$\Theta_{\cA} = \kappa \cdot \eta \otimes \Lambda$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:explicit-theta}) either vanishes
identically or is nonzero at every genus.
The MC equation couples all genera simultaneously ---
there is no mechanism for $\Theta$ to ``turn off'' at a
single genus while remaining active elsewhere.
Anomaly cancellation ($\kappa = 0$) is the homotopy-algebraic
incarnation: the bar complex is uncurved precisely when the
universal MC element is trivial.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[\texorpdfstring{$\kappa$}{kappa} as Chern--Simons level]\label{rem:kappa-chern-simons}
\index{obstruction coefficient!Chern--Simons interpretation}
\index{Chern--Simons theory!obstruction coefficient}
For affine Kac--Moody $\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k$, the obstruction coefficient $\kappa = (k+h^\vee)d/(2h^\vee)$ is proportional to the shifted level $t = k + h^\vee$, which is the level of the associated 3d Chern--Simons theory.  The genus-$g$ free energy $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{FP}$ then becomes a tautological integral over $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ weighted by the Chern--Simons level.  This connects the bar-complex obstruction theory to the Witten--Reshetikhin--Turaev invariants of 3-manifolds: the free energy $\sum_g F_g \hbar^{2g-2}$ is the asymptotic expansion of the Chern--Simons partition function on $\Sigma_g \times S^1$.
The universal MC class
$\Theta_{\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_k}^{\min} =
\frac{t \cdot d}{2h^\vee}\,\eta \otimes \Lambda$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:explicit-theta}) is proportional to
$t = k + h^\vee$, the Chern--Simons level: the
bar-complex curvature is the homotopy-algebraic shadow of the
Chern--Simons action, and $\Theta = 0$ at critical level
recovers the uncurved phase where the CS partition function is
topological.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch bridge; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{prop:grr-bridge}
\index{Grothendieck--Riemann--Roch!genus expansion}
\index{Hodge bundle!genus expansion}
The genus generating function of any modular Koszul chiral algebra
$\cA$ is a Hodge integral:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grr-bridge}
F_g(\cA) \;=\; \kappa(\cA) \cdot
\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}} \psi_1^{2g-2}\, c_g(\mathbb{E}),
\end{equation}
where $\mathbb{E}$ is the Hodge bundle and $\psi_1$ is the
cotangent line class.  The total generating function
\begin{equation}\label{eq:grr-bridge-total}
\sum_{g \geq 1} F_g(\cA)\, x^{2g}
\;=\; \kappa(\cA) \cdot
\sum_{g \geq 1}
\left(\int_{\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{g,1}}
\psi^{2g-2}\, c_g(\mathbb{E})\right) x^{2g}
\;=\;
\kappa(\cA) \cdot \Bigl(\frac{x/2}{\sin(x/2)} - 1\Bigr)
\end{equation}
is an explicit Hodge integral series, whose closed form
$(x/2)/\sin(x/2)$ is the Wick rotation of the $\hat{A}$-genus
\textup{(}Remark~\textup{\ref{rem:A-hat-genus})}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Equation~\eqref{eq:grr-bridge} combines
Theorem~\ref{thm:genus-universality} ($\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot
\lambda_g$, $F_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}}$) with
the Faber--Pandharipande formula
(Theorem~\ref{thm:mumford-formula}):
$\lambda_g^{\mathrm{FP}} = \int \psi^{2g-2}\, c_g(\mathbb{E})$.
Equation~\eqref{eq:grr-bridge-total} follows from
Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-generating-function}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Family index theorem]\label{rem:towards-family-index}
\index{index theorem!modular deformation}
The family index theorem (Theorem~\ref{thm:family-index}) assembles
$\sum F_g x^{2g}=\kappa(\cA)(\hat{A}(ix)-1)$ as the GRR
pushforward of the Todd class of the universal curve, with
$\mathcal{D}_{\cA}^{(g)}=\kappa\cdot\mathbb{E}$ determined by
genus universality.  Constructing $\mathcal{D}_{\cA}^{(g)}$ as a
sheaf requires the coderived Ran-space formalism
(Theorem~\ref{thm:universal-MC}).
\end{remark}

% ================================================================
% SECTION 4.14: COMPLEMENTARITY THEOREM
% ================================================================

\section{The complementarity theorem}
\label{sec:complementarity-theorem}

\subsection{Physical and mathematical motivation}

\begin{remark}[Physical perspective: Witten's insight]
In conformal field theory, consider a chiral algebra $\mathcal{A}$ and compute its
partition function on a genus-$g$ Riemann surface $\Sigma_g$:
\begin{equation}
Z_g[\mathcal{A}] = \int_{\mathcal{M}_g} \langle \mathcal{A} \rangle_{\Sigma_g} 
\cdot e^{-S[\Sigma_g]}
\end{equation}

At genus $g \geq 1$, quantum corrections split into deformations (marginal operators) and obstructions (anomalies).
The complementarity theorem asserts: \emph{what $\mathcal{A}$ sees as obstruction,
its Koszul dual $\mathcal{A}^!$ sees as deformation, and vice versa}.

\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Kodaira--Spencer action on tautological classes]
The center $Z(\cA)$ acts on $H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g)$
($\lambda$-classes, $\psi$-classes, boundary classes) via the
Kodaira--Spencer map
$\rho\colon Z(\cA)\to\mathrm{End}(H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g))$,
and the eigenspace decomposition gives
$H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g,Z(\cA))
=Q_g(\cA)\oplus Q_g(\cA^!)$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Algebraic perspective: Grothendieck's functoriality]
Since $(\mathcal{A}^!)^! \simeq \mathcal{A}$, any functor on Koszul pairs must satisfy $F(\mathcal{A}) \oplus F(\mathcal{A}^!) = \text{universal object}$.  The complementarity theorem identifies this universal object as $H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, Z(\mathcal{A}))$: the decomposition is direct, exhaustive, and functorial.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Computational perspective: Heisenberg at genus~$1$]
For $\mathcal{H}_\kappa$ at genus~$1$:
$H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_{1,1})=\mathbb{Q}\oplus\mathbb{Q}\lambda$,
$Q_1(\mathcal{H}_\kappa)=\mathbb{C}\cdot\kappa$ (central extension),
$Q_1(\mathcal{H}_\kappa^!)=\mathbb{C}\cdot\lambda$ (curved structure),
and $Q_1\oplus Q_1^!=H^0\oplus H^2=\mathbb{C}^2$.
\end{remark}

\subsection{Statement of the theorem}

\begin{definition}[Deformation-obstruction complexes: H-level]
\label{def:complementarity-complexes}
\index{deformation-obstruction complexes|textbf}
Let $(\cA, \cA^!)$ be a chiral Koszul pair on~$X$.
The \emph{ambient complex} at genus~$g$ is
\[
\mathbf{C}_g(\cA) := R\Gamma(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA)),
\]
where $\mathcal{Z}(\cA)$ is the center local system.
The Verdier involution $\sigma$ acts on $\mathbf{C}_g(\cA)$ as a
cochain-level endomorphism with $\sigma^2 = \mathrm{id}$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:verdier-bar-cobar}).
Define the \emph{deformation-obstruction complexes} as homotopy eigenspaces:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:complementarity-fiber}
\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA) := \operatorname{fib}(\sigma - \mathrm{id}\colon
\mathbf{C}_g \to \mathbf{C}_g), \qquad
\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA^!) := \operatorname{fib}(\sigma + \mathrm{id}\colon
\mathbf{C}_g \to \mathbf{C}_g).
\end{equation}
The \emph{cohomological shadows} (S-level) are defined by:
\begin{align}\label{eq:shadow-spaces}
Q_g(\cA) &:= H^*(\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA))
= \ker(\sigma - \mathrm{id} \mid H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))),\\
Q_g(\cA^!) &:= H^*(\mathbf{Q}_g(\cA^!))
= \ker(\sigma + \mathrm{id} \mid H^*(\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g, \mathcal{Z}(\cA))).
\end{align}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[H/M/S layers; Convention~\ref{conv:hms-levels}]
The homotopy fibers~\eqref{eq:complementarity-fiber} are the
H-level objects; the explicit cochain models
$(\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA), \Dg{g})$ are the M-level presentations; and
the kernel decomposition~\eqref{eq:shadow-spaces} is the S-level
shadow.  The standard involution-splitting lemma in characteristic~$0$
(an involution on a complex splits it into homotopy eigenspaces whose
direct sum recovers the original) makes the passage from H to S
automatic.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Involution splitting in characteristic~\texorpdfstring{$0$}{0}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:involution-splitting}
\index{involution splitting lemma|textbf}
Let $V$ be a cochain complex over a field of characteristic $\neq 2$,
and let $\sigma \colon V \to V$ be a cochain involution
($\sigma^2 = \mathrm{id}$, $\sigma \circ d = d \circ \sigma$).  Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item The homotopy eigenspaces
  $V^+ := \operatorname{fib}(\sigma - \mathrm{id})$ and
  $V^- := \operatorname{fib}(\sigma + \mathrm{id})$
  split $V$ in the homotopy category:
  $V^+ \oplus V^- \xrightarrow{\;\sim\;} V$.
\item On cohomology:
  $H^*(V) = \ker(\sigma - \mathrm{id}) \oplus \ker(\sigma + \mathrm{id})$.
\item If $\langle -,- \rangle$ is a cochain-level pairing on~$V$
  with $\langle \sigma x, \sigma y \rangle = -\langle x, y \rangle$
  \textup{(}anti-symmetric under $\sigma$\textup{)}, then $V^+$ and
  $V^-$ are isotropic for $\langle -,- \rangle$; if the pairing is
  non-degenerate, they are Lagrangian.
\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The projectors $p^\pm := \tfrac{1}{2}(\mathrm{id} \pm \sigma)$
are cochain maps with $p^+ + p^- = \mathrm{id}$,
$(p^\pm)^2 = p^\pm$, and $p^+ \circ p^- = 0$.
Part~(a): the inclusion $\operatorname{im}(p^+) \oplus \operatorname{im}(p^-)
\hookrightarrow V$ is a quasi-isomorphism by direct-sum decomposition,
and $\operatorname{im}(p^\pm) \simeq \operatorname{fib}(\sigma \mp \mathrm{id})$
via the standard cone identification.
Part~(b) follows by applying $H^*$ to~(a).
Part~(c): for $x, y \in V^+$ we have $\sigma x = x$, $\sigma y = y$,
so $\langle x, y \rangle = \langle \sigma x, \sigma y \rangle
= -\langle x, y \rangle$, hence $\langle x, y \rangle = 0$.
Maximality is immediate from the direct-sum decomposition.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Relative bar fiber complex]\label{def:relative-bar-fiber}
\index{bar complex!relative fiber|textbf}
Let $(\cA, \cA^!)$ be a chiral Koszul pair on~$X$, and let
\[
\pi_g\colon \mathcal{C}_g(\cA) \longrightarrow
\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g
\]
be the family of genus-$g$ compactified configuration spaces
carrying the relative bar complex $\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$.
Its stalk at $[\Sigma] \in \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ is the
\emph{genus-$g$ fiber bar complex}
$C^{(g)}_X(\cA)\!\mid_\Sigma$, i.e.\ the bar complex of~$\cA$
on the fixed curve~$\Sigma$ with the fiberwise curved
differential~$\dfib$
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:higher-genus-differentials})}.
\end{definition}

\begin{lemma}[Perfectness criterion for the relative bar family;
\ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{lem:perfectness-criterion}
\index{perfectness criterion|textbf}
\index{bar complex!relative perfectness|textbf}
Let $(\cA, \cA^!)$ be a chiral Koszul pair on a smooth projective
curve~$X$, carrying a modular pre-Koszul datum
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral})}.
Suppose the following two conditions hold:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \emph{PBW filterability.}
  The genus-$g$ bar complex $\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$ admits an
  exhaustive multiplicative filtration~$F_\bullet$ such that the
  associated graded $\operatorname{gr}_F \bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$
  sees only the genus-$0$ collision differential~$\dzero$ and is
  Koszul-acyclic \textup{(}axioms \textup{MK1} and
  \textup{MK3} of
  Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral})}.

\item \emph{Finite-dimensional fiber cohomology.}
  For each closed point
  $[\Sigma] \in \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$,
  $\dim_\mathbb{C} H^n\bigl(
  \bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)\big|_\Sigma\bigr)
  < \infty$ for all~$n$.
\end{enumerate}
Then the derived pushforward
$R\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$ is a perfect complex on
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The argument has three steps.

\emph{Step~1: Uniform cohomological bound from the associated graded.}
The PBW filtration~$F_\bullet$ is flat over the base
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$ (it is a bar-degree filtration,
hence defined fiber-by-fiber by the combinatorial bar grading).
At the associated graded level the fiberwise
curvature $\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_g$ vanishes
(it sits in positive filtration degree), so
$\operatorname{gr}_F$ carries only the genus-$0$
differential~$\dzero$.  By Koszul acyclicity~(i), the
cohomology of $\operatorname{gr}_F$ is concentrated in total
degree~$0$, giving a uniform vanishing range
$H^q(\operatorname{gr}_F\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)\big|_\Sigma) = 0$
for $q \neq 0$ at every point of the base.

\emph{Step~2: Transfer to the filtered complex.}
The bar-degree filtration spectral sequence
$E_1^{p,q} =
H^q(\operatorname{gr}_p\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)\big|_\Sigma)$
has $E_1^{p,q} = 0$ for $q \neq 0$ by Step~1.  All higher
differentials $d_r$ ($r \geq 1$) therefore vanish (they map into
or out of the zero row), and the spectral sequence collapses at
$E_1$ with $E_\infty^{p,q} = E_1^{p,q}$.  In particular, the
full fiber complex $\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)\big|_\Sigma$ has
cohomology concentrated in degree~$0$ for every~$\Sigma$.
The uniform vanishing range $q \neq 0$ is independent
of~$[\Sigma]$.

\emph{Step~3: Cohomology and base change.}
The family
$\pi_g\colon \mathcal{C}_g(\cA) \to \overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$
is a proper morphism of finite type.  By Steps~1--2, the fiber
cohomology sheaves $R^q\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$ vanish for
$q \neq 0$ uniformly over the base, and the surviving $R^0$ has
finite-dimensional fibers by hypothesis~(ii).  The standard
cohomology and base change theorem
(EGA~III, Th\'eor\`eme~7.7.5)
then gives that $R\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$ is a perfect
complex (bounded, with coherent cohomology sheaves) on
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Fiber--center identification \textup{(Theorem~\texorpdfstring{$\mathrm{C}_0$}{C0})}; \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:fiber-center-identification}
\index{fiber--center identification|textbf}
\textup{[}Regime: curved-central
\textup{(}Convention~\textup{\ref{conv:regime-tags})].}

\smallskip\noindent
Assume $\cA$ carries a modular pre-Koszul datum
\textup{(}Definition~\textup{\ref{def:modular-koszul-chiral})}
with finite-dimensional fiber cohomology, so that the relative bar
family $R\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)$ is perfect over
$\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$
\textup{(}Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:perfectness-criterion})}.
Then:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:fiber-center}
R^q\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA) = 0
\quad\text{for } q \neq 0,
\qquad
R^0\pi_{g*}\bar{B}^{(g)}(\cA)
\;\cong\; \mathcal{Z}_{\cA}
\end{equation}
as local systems/sheaves on $\overline{\mathcal{M}}_g$,
where $\mathcal{Z}_{\cA}$ is the center local system.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof proceeds in four steps.

\emph{Step~1: Filter.}
Filter the full fiber bar complex
$C^{(g)}_X(\cA)\!\mid_\Sigma$ by bar degree, writing
\[
F_p := \bigoplus_{n \leq p} \bar{B}^{(g),n}(\cA).
\]

\emph{Step~2: Identify the associated graded.}
At the associated graded level, the fiberwise curvature
$\dfib^{\,2} = \kappa(\cA)\cdot\omega_g$ vanishes (it lies
in positive filtration degree), so $\operatorname{gr}_F$ sees
only the genus-$0$ collision differential~$\dzero$.
